     <p><b>University of Washington</b> (<b>UW</b>), commonly referred to as <b>Washington</b> or informally <b>UDub</b>, is a public research university in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" title="Washington (U.S. state)" class="mw-redirect">Washington</a>, United States. Founded in 1861, UW is one of the oldest universities on the West Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has three campuses: the largest in the <a href="/wiki/University_District,_Seattle" title="University District, Seattle">University District</a> (Seattle) and two others in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Tacoma" title="University of Washington Tacoma">Tacoma</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Bothell" title="University of Washington Bothell">Bothell</a>. Its operating expenses and research budget for fiscal year 2012 totaled more than US$ 7.2 billion <sup id="cite_ref-UW_Budget_Office_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_Budget_Office-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The UW occupies over 500 buildings, with over 20 million gross square footage of space, including the latest <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Plaza" title="University of Washington Plaza">University of Washington Plaza</a> consisting of the 325&nbsp;ft UW Tower and conference center.</p> 
     <p>The University of Washington has been called a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> institution and is an elected member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Universities" title="American Association of Universities" class="mw-redirect">American Association of Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's research budget is among the highest in the United States. It enjoys a high evaluation in various global <a href="/wiki/University_rankings" title="University rankings" class="mw-redirect">university rankings</a> as well.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghairanking1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghairanking1-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QS_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THE_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In athletics, the university competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a> (Pac-12).</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The city of Seattle was one of several settlements in the mid to late 19th century vying for primacy in the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Washington_Territory" title="Washington Territory">Washington Territory</a>. In 1854, territorial governor <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Stevens" title="Isaac Stevens">Isaac Stevens</a> recommended the establishment of a university in <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>. Several prominent Seattle-area residents, chief among them <a href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist" class="mw-redirect">Methodist</a> preacher Daniel Bagley, saw the siting of this University as a chance to add to the city's prestige. They were able to convince early founder of Seattle and member of the territorial legislature <a href="/wiki/Arthur_A._Denny" title="Arthur A. Denny">Arthur A. Denny</a> of the importance of Seattle winning the school. The legislature initially chartered two universities, one in Seattle and one in <a href="/wiki/Lewis_County,_Washington" title="Lewis County, Washington">Lewis County</a>, but later repealed its decision in favor of a single university in Lewis County, provided locally donated land could be found. When no site emerged, the legislature, encouraged by Denny, relocated the university to Seattle in 1858.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/220px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/330px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/df/Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg/440px-Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_University_of_Washington_-_c1870.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The original University of Washington building on Denny's Knoll, 
        <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1870
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1861, scouting began for an appropriate 10 acres (4&nbsp;ha) site in Seattle to serve as the campus for a new university. Denny, along with fellow pioneers Edward Lander and Charlie Terry, donated a site on &quot;Denny's Knoll&quot; in <a href="/wiki/Downtown,_Seattle,_Washington" title="Downtown, Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">downtown Seattle</a>. This tract was bounded by 4th and 6th Avenues on the west and east and Union and Seneca Streets on the north and south.</p> 
     <p>UW opened officially on November 4, 1861, as the <b>Territorial University of Washington</b>. The following year, the legislature passed articles formally incorporating the University and establishing a Board of Regents. The school struggled initially, closing three times: in 1863 for lack of students, and again in 1867 and 1876 due to shortage of funds. However, <a href="/wiki/Clara_Antoinette_McCarty_Wilt" title="Clara Antoinette McCarty Wilt">Clara Antoinette McCarty Wilt</a> became the first graduate of UW in 1876 when she graduated from UW with a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degree</a> in science. By the time Washington entered the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> in 1889, both Seattle and the University had grown substantially. Enrollment had increased from an initial 30 students to nearly 300, and the relative isolation of the campus had given way to encroaching development. A special legislative committee headed by UW graduate <a href="/wiki/Edmond_Meany" title="Edmond Meany" class="mw-redirect">Edmond Meany</a> was created for the purpose of finding a new campus better able to serve the growing student population. The committee selected a site on <a href="/wiki/Union_Bay_(Seattle,_Washington)" title="Union Bay (Seattle, Washington)" class="mw-redirect">Union Bay</a> northeast of <a href="/wiki/Downtown,_Seattle,_Washington" title="Downtown, Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">downtown</a>, and the legislature appropriated funds for its purchase and subsequent construction.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/220px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/330px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg/440px-Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Alaska_Yukon_Pacific_Exposition_-_Rainier_Vista.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Alaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition on the UW campus toward 
        <a href="/wiki/Mount_Rainier" title="Mount Rainier">Mount Rainier</a> in 1909
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University relocated from downtown to the new campus in 1895, moving into the newly built Denny Hall. The regents tried and failed to sell the old campus, and eventually settled on leasing the area. The University still owns what is now called the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Tract_(Seattle)" title="Metropolitan Tract (Seattle)">Metropolitan Tract</a>. In the heart of the city, it is among the most valuable pieces of real estate in Seattle and generates millions of US$ in revenue annually.</p> 
     <p>The original Territorial University building was torn down in 1908 and its former site currently houses the Fairmont Olympic Hotel. The sole surviving remnants of UW's first building are four 24-foot (7.3&nbsp;m), white, hand-fluted cedar, Ionic columns. They were salvaged by <a href="/wiki/Edmond_S._Meany" title="Edmond S. Meany">Edmond S. Meany</a>?one of the University's first graduates and the former head of the history department. Meany and his colleague, Dean Herbert T. Condon, dubbed each of the columns &quot;Loyalty,&quot; &quot;Industry,&quot; &quot;Faith&quot; and &quot;Efficiency,&quot; or &quot;LIFE.&quot; The columns now stand in the Sylvan Grove Theater.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Organizers of the 1909 <a href="/wiki/Alaska-Yukon-Pacific_Exposition" title="Alaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition" class="mw-redirect">Alaska-Yukon-Pacific Exposition</a> eyed the still largely undeveloped campus as a prime setting for their <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" title="World's Fair" class="mw-redirect">world's fair</a>. They came to an agreement with the Board of Regents that allowed them to use the campus grounds for the exposition. In exchange, the University would be able to take advantage of the development of the campus for the fair after its conclusion. This included a detailed site plan and several buildings. The plan for the A-Y-P Exposition prepared by <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Olmsted" title="John Charles Olmsted">John Charles Olmsted</a> was later incorporated into the overall campus master plan and permanently affected the layout of the campus.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uwaerial1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/220px-Uwaerial1922.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/330px-Uwaerial1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Uwaerial1922.jpg/440px-Uwaerial1922.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uwaerial1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An aerial view of the University campus, dating from 1922 or before
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Both <a href="/wiki/World_War" title="World War" class="mw-redirect">World Wars</a> brought the military to the campus, with certain facilities temporarily loaned to the federal government. The subsequent post-war periods were times of dramatic growth for the University.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The period between the wars saw significant expansion on the upper campus. Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts" class="mw-redirect">liberal arts</a> <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangle</a>, known to students as &quot;The Quad,&quot; began in 1916 and continued in stages until 1939. The first two wings of <a href="/wiki/Suzzallo_Library" title="Suzzallo Library">Suzzallo Library</a>, considered the architectural centerpiece of the University, were built in 1926 and 1935, respectively. Further growth came with the end of World War II and passage of the <a href="/wiki/G._I._Bill_of_Rights" title="G. I. Bill of Rights" class="mw-redirect">G.I. Bill</a>. Among the most important developments of this period was the opening of the medical school in 1946. It would eventually grow into the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Medical_Center" title="University of Washington Medical Center">University of Washington Medical Center</a>, now ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> among the top ten hospitals in the United States. It was during this era in University of Washington history in which many Japanese Americans were sent away from the university to <a href="/wiki/Internment_camps" title="Internment camps" class="mw-redirect">internment camps</a> along the West-coast of the United States as part of <a href="/wiki/Executive_Order_9066" title="Executive Order 9066">Executive Order 9066</a> following the attacks on <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>. As a result, many Japanese American &quot;soon-to-be&quot; graduates were unable to receive their diplomas and be recognized for their accomplishment at the university until the University of Washington's commemoration ceremony for the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Americans" title="Japanese Americans" class="mw-redirect">Japanese Americans</a> entitled <a href="/wiki/The_Long_Journey_Home" title="The Long Journey Home">The Long Journey Home</a> held on May 18, 2008 at the main campus.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gasworks_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gasworks_Park.JPG/220px-Gasworks_Park.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gasworks_Park.JPG/330px-Gasworks_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gasworks_Park.JPG/440px-Gasworks_Park.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Gasworks_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of University of Washington and Gas Works Park from George Washington Memorial Bridge in 2008
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the late 1960s, the University of Washington Police Department evolved from the University Safety and Security Division in response to anti-Vietnam War protests.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> It currently has jurisdiction over the University of Washington campus and University-owned housing, except for the Radford Court apartments in <a href="/wiki/Sand_Point,_Seattle,_Washington" title="Sand Point, Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">Sand Point</a>. The 1960s and 1970s are known as the &quot;golden age&quot; of the university due to the tremendous growth in students, facilities, operating budget and prestige under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Odegaard" title="Charles Odegaard">Charles Odegaard</a> from 1958 to 1973. Enrollment at UW more than doubled?from around 16,000 to 34,000?as the <a href="/wiki/Post-WW2_baby_boom" title="Post-WW2 baby boom" class="mw-redirect">baby boom</a> generation came of age. As was the case at many American universities, this era was marked by high levels of <a href="/wiki/Student_activism" title="Student activism">student activism</a>, with much of the unrest focused around <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights" title="Civil rights" class="mw-redirect">civil rights</a> and opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Odegaard instituted a vision of building a &quot;community of scholars&quot; and convinced the state of Washington legislatures to increase their investments towards the university. Additionally, Washington <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">senators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_M._Jackson" title="Henry M. Jackson">Henry M. Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Magnuson" title="Warren G. Magnuson" class="mw-redirect">Warren G. Magnuson</a> used their political clout to funnel federal research monies to the University of Washington and to this day, UW is among the top recipients of federal research funds in the United States. The results included an operating budget increase of $37 million in 1958, to over $400 million in 1973, and 35 new buildings that doubled the floor space of the university.</p> 
     <p>The University opened campuses in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington,_Bothell" title="University of Washington, Bothell" class="mw-redirect">Bothell</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington,_Tacoma" title="University of Washington, Tacoma" class="mw-redirect">Tacoma</a> in 1990. Initially, these campuses offered curricula for students seeking <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">bachelor's degrees</a> who have already completed two years of higher education, but both schools have transitioned to four-year universities, accepting the first freshman class in the fall of 2006. Both campuses offer master's degree programs as well. In 2009 the University opened an office in the Spanish city of <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Spain" title="Le&oacute;n, Spain">Le&oacute;n</a> in collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="University of Le&oacute;n">local university</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="Campus of the University of Washington">Campus of the University of Washington</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Washington_Quad,_Spring_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/220px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/330px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg/440px-University_of_Washington_Quad%2C_Spring_2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Washington_Quad,_Spring_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Quad, University of Washington
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Washington, Seattle campus, is situated on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Union_Bay_(Seattle,_Washington)" title="Union Bay (Seattle, Washington)" class="mw-redirect">Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portage_Bay" title="Portage Bay">Portage Bays</a>, with views of the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> to the east and the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Mountains" title="Olympic Mountains">Olympic Mountains</a> to the west. The main campus is bounded on the west by 15th Avenue N.E., on the north by N.E. 45th Street, on the east by Montlake Boulevard N.E., and on the south by N.E. Pacific Street. East Campus stretches east of Montlake Boulevard to <a href="/wiki/Laurelhurst,_Seattle,_Washington" title="Laurelhurst, Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">Laurelhurst</a> and is largely taken up by <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> and sports fields. South Campus occupies the land between Pacific Street and the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Washington_Ship_Canal" title="Lake Washington Ship Canal">Lake Washington Ship Canal</a> which used to be a <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf course</a> and is given over to the <a href="/wiki/Health_sciences" title="Health sciences" class="mw-redirect">health sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">oceanography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fisheries_science" title="Fisheries science">fisheries</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Medical_Center" title="University of Washington Medical Center">University of Washington Medical Center</a>. West Campus is less of a separate entity than the others, many of its facilities being on city streets, and stretches between 15th Avenue and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a> from the Ship Canal to N.E. 41st Street. University Way, known locally as &quot;<a href="/wiki/The_Ave" title="The Ave">The Ave</a>&quot;, lies nearby and is a focus for much student life at the university. At the heart of the university lies Red Square, which functions as the central hub of student interaction and hosts a variety of events annually.</p> 
     <p>Several major motion picture films were filmed on campus or used it as a backdrop, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sixth_Man" title="The Sixth Man" class="mw-redirect">The Sixth Man</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-SixthMan_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SixthMan-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/WarGames" title="WarGames">WarGames</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-WarGamesFilming_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarGamesFilming-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/What_the_Bleep!%3F:_Down_the_Rabbit_Hole" title="What the Bleep!?: Down the Rabbit Hole" class="mw-redirect">What the Bleep!?: Down the Rabbit Hole</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-WhatTheBleepFilming_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhatTheBleepFilming-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/21_and_Over_(film)" title="21 and Over (film)" class="mw-redirect">21 and Over</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21andOver_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21andOver-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Washington_Presidents" title="List of University of Washington Presidents">List of University of Washington Presidents</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The current President of the University of Washington is <a href="/wiki/Michael_K._Young" title="Michael K. Young">Michael K. Young</a>. Phyllis Wise, who had previously served as Provost and Executive Vice President and for a year as Interim President, was named the Chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana-Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign" class="mw-redirect">University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign</a> in August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University is governed by ten regents, one of whom is a student. Its most notable current regent is likely <a href="/wiki/William_H._Gates,_Sr." title="William H. Gates, Sr.">William H. Gates, Sr.</a>, father of <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a>. The undergraduate student government is the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Students_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="Associated Students of the University of Washington">Associated Students of the University of Washington</a> (ASUW) and the graduate student government is the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Senate" title="Graduate and Professional Student Senate">Graduate and Professional Student Senate</a> (GPSS).</p> 
     <p>The University offers bachelor's, master's and <a href="/wiki/Doctoral_degree" title="Doctoral degree" class="mw-redirect">doctoral</a> degrees through its 140 departments, themselves organized into various colleges and schools:<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td valign="top"> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="University of Washington College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Henry_M._Jackson_School_of_International_Studies" title="University of Washington Henry M. Jackson School of International Studies">Henry M. Jackson School of International Studies</a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_College_of_Built_Environments" title="University of Washington College of Built Environments">College of Built Environments</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Business_School" title="University of Washington Business School" class="mw-redirect">Michael G. Foster School of Business</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_School_of_Dentistry" title="University of Washington School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a></li> 
          <li>College of Education</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_College_of_Engineering" title="University of Washington College of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">College of Engineering</a></li> 
          <li>College of the Environment</li> 
          <li>The Graduate School</li> 
         </ul> </td> 
        <td valign="top">

          <li>School of Social Work</li> 
         </ul> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics_and_research">Academics and research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Academics and research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/220px-Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/330px-Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/440px-Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Suzzallo Library, University of Washington
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2006, the University of Washington research budget passed the $1.0 billion milestone.<sup id="cite_ref-UW_.241_billion_research_mark_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_.241_billion_research_mark-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Virtually all of the funding came from peer-reviewed research proposals. UW research budget consistently ranks among the top 5 in both public and private universities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-UW_Annual_Report_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_Annual_Report-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-top_research_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top_research-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> UW is also the largest recipient of federal research funding among public universities and second among all public and private universities in the country, a position that the university has held each year since 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is an elected member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg/220px-U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg/330px-U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg/440px-U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:U._of_Wash_Quad_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> School of Art, University of Washington

     <p>UW students include 136 Fulbright Scholars, 35 Rhodes Scholars, 7 Marshall Scholars and 4 Gates Cambridge Scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> For Fall 2012, the University of Washington admitted about 59% of applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the 2011?12 autumn term, the university had 42,428 students, making it the largest university (in terms of student population) on the west coast.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, the average unweighted high school GPA of incoming freshmen was 3.78, and the average <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> score was 1790.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> About 33% of all undergraduates are members of <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minority groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Washington recruits faculty and staff from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the faculty, there are 151 members of American Association for the Advancement of Science, 68 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 67 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, 53 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, 6 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates, 2 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, 1 winner of the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>, 29 winners of the Presidential Early Career Awards in Science and Engineering, 15 Howard Hughes Medical Institute Investigators, 15 <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows" title="MacArthur Fellows" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellows</a>, 9 winners of the <a href="/wiki/Gairdner_Foundation_International_Award" title="Gairdner Foundation International Award">Gairdner Foundation International Award</a>, 5 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, 5 winners of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Lasker_Award_for_Clinical_Medical_Research" title="Albert Lasker Award for Clinical Medical Research" class="mw-redirect">Albert Lasker Award for Clinical Medical Research</a>, 4 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>, 2 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Award" title="National Book Award">National Book Award</a>, and 2 winners of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" title="National Medal of Arts">National Medal of Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In May 2010, the University of Washington's six Nobel laureates were honoured by <a href="/wiki/Crown_Princess_Victoria_of_Sweden" title="Crown Princess Victoria of Sweden" class="mw-redirect">Crown Princess Victoria of Sweden</a>, at a special dinner held in Seattle. They are <a href="/wiki/Hans_Georg_Dehmelt" title="Hans Georg Dehmelt">Hans Georg Dehmelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/E._Donnall_Thomas" title="E. Donnall Thomas">E. Donnall Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_G._Krebs" title="Edwin G. Krebs">Edwin G. Krebs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Fisher" title="Edmund Fisher">Edmund Fisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leland_Hartwell" title="Leland Hartwell" class="mw-redirect">Leland Hartwell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linda_Buck" title="Linda Buck" class="mw-redirect">Linda Buck</a>. The event was organized by Seattle?s Swedish Consulate as part of ?Sweden Week?.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg/220px-Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg/330px-Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg/440px-Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Seattle_-_Portage_Bay_Place_E_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> South Campus, University of Washington
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Libraries" title="University of Washington Libraries">University of Washington library system</a> is the 18th largest library in the United States, with holdings of more than 7.5 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The Association of Research Libraries ranked the UW library system between the top fifth and fifteenth in various categories.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UW is also the host university of <a href="/wiki/ResearchChannel" title="ResearchChannel" class="mw-redirect">ResearchChannel</a> program, the only TV channel in the United States dedicated solely for the dissemination of research from academic institutions and research organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-ResearchChannel_host_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchChannel_host-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Current participation of ResearchChannel includes 36 universities, 15 research organizations, two corporate research centers and many other affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-ResearchChannel_participants_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ResearchChannel_participants-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> UW also disseminates knowledge through its proprietary UWTV channel and online.<sup id="cite_ref-UWTV_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWTV-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/220px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/330px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg/440px-Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_of_Suzzallo_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Entrance of Suzzallo Library, University of Washington
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>To promote equal academic opportunity, especially for people of low income, UW launched <i>Husky Promise</i> in 2006. Families of income up to 65 percent of state median income or 235 percent of federal poverty level are eligible. With this, up to 30 percent of undergraduate students may be eligible. The cut-off income level that UW set is the highest in the nation, making top quality education available to more people. Then UW President, Mark Emmert, simply said that being &quot;elitist is not in our DNA&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Inside_HigherEd_Husky_Promise_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inside_HigherEd_Husky_Promise-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UW_Husky_Promise_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UW_Husky_Promise-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;Last year, the University of Washington moved to a more comprehensive approach [to admissions], in which the admissions staff reads the entire application and looks at grades within the context of the individual high school, rather than relying on computerized cutoffs.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 1977, there has been a <a href="/wiki/Transition_School_and_Early_Entrance_Program" title="Transition School and Early Entrance Program">Transition School and Early Entrance Program</a> on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-eep_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eep-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;The Early Entrance Program is the Robinson Center?s original early university entrance program. Recognized as one of the most prestigious early university entrance programs in the nation, this program facilitates early entry to the University of Washington for a carefully selected group of sixteen highly-capable young students younger than fifteen (15) years old. As mandated by state law, students must have completed 6th grade in order to enroll in the Transition School.&quot; This Robinson Center also has a program called the UW <a href="/wiki/Academy_for_Young_Scholars" title="Academy for Young Scholars">Academy for Young Scholars</a>: &quot;The UW Academy is the premier early university entrance program for high school students in Washington State. A small cohort of up to thirty-five academically advanced and highly motivated students are admitted to the UW Academy each year. Students apply to the UW Academy during their 10th grade year, and if accepted, withdraw from high school at the end of 10th grade to enroll as freshmen at the University of Washington.&quot; All Academy students are automatically admitted into the UW Honors Program.</p>

     <p>In the most recent international rankings: University of Washington ranked 16th among the world top 500 universities by <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) and has been consistently regarded to be among the top 20 by the institution. <sup id="cite_ref-shanghairanking1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghairanking1-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> (2012-13), the institute ranked 25th worldwide <sup id="cite_ref-THE_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> when its <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings#World_Reputation_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">World Reputation Rankings</a> of the same year considered it to be 26th.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> (2012) ranked it 59th globally.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For local rankings: <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a> ranked UW's undergraduate program 42nd among &quot;national universities&quot; and 10th among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Among graduate programs, in 2012 <i>U.S. News</i> ranked UW's program in primary care medicine first,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a> first,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social work</a> third,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> pharmacy fifth,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Library_and_information_science" title="Library and information science">library and information science</a> fourth,<sup id="cite_ref-Library_and_Information_School_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_and_Information_School-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> sixth,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> computer science seventh,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> education seventh,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> research medicine ninth,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> engineering 21st,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and law 20th.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> UW's nursing school has ranked first each year in the <i>U.S. News</i> rankings since the magazine began ranking nursing schools in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i> National University Rankings, University of Washington ranked 8th in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> 16th in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> 14th in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> 14th in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> and 15th in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The Top American Research Universities ranked University of Washington 11th among the top 50 American universities in 2010 published by <a href="/wiki/The_Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="The Center for Measuring University Performance" class="mw-redirect">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Rankings published by institutions of other places: Leiden Ranking (2013) published by Leiden University of Netherlands ranked University of Washington 27th among the world 500 major universities.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, University of Washington ranked 8th among the world 2,000 universities in <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance" class="mw-redirect">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a> (URAP) published by <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Technical_University" title="Middle East Technical University">Middle East Technical University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, the Top 200 Colleges and Universities in the World on University Web Ranking published by 4 International Colleges &amp; Universitiesr placed it at 8th.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>There are rankings for some specific domains as well. It ranked 13th among 300 Best World Universities in 2011 compiled by <a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a> (HRLR) on Measurements of World's Top 300 Universities Graduates' Performance .<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> magazine's 2012 &quot;Best Values in Public Colleges&quot; list, the university ranked 14th for in-state students and 18th for out-of-state students<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the university ranked second among universities by number of undergraduate alumni currently serving as <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> volunteers, at 110.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> UW tied for third in 2010 (94 volunteers),<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> first in 2009 (101 volunteers),<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> first in 2008 (104 volunteers)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and first in 2007 (113 volunteers).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">Global Language Monitor</a>'s rankings of universities by Internet presence, UW ranked 12th in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/SmartMoney" title="SmartMoney">SmartMoney</a> named the University of Washington as 6th best salary returns on tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The student newspaper is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_of_the_University_of_Washington" title="The Daily of the University of Washington">The Daily of the University of Washington</a></i>, usually referred to as simply <i>The Daily</i>. It is the second largest daily in Seattle and is published every day classes are in session during fall, winter and spring quarters, and weekly during summer quarter. In 2010, <i>The Daily</i> launched a half-hour weekly television magazine show, &quot;The Daily's Double Shot,&quot; broadcast <a href="/wiki/UWTV" title="UWTV" class="mw-redirect">UWTV</a>, Channel 27.</p> 
     <p>The Beta (second) chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a> collegiate philanthropic-social organization for women was established at the university in 1929.</p> 
     <p>The IMA Center for <a href="/wiki/Intramural_sports" title="Intramural sports">intramural sports</a> was built in 1968. A $41 million remodel and expansion project began 2001 and the building was reopened in fall 2003 with a 95,000 square feet (8,800&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) addition to its northwest to the original 40,000 square feet (3,700&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) facility.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> North of the building, the project eliminated three of the nine outdoor tennis courts with the expansion, but included an all-weather <a href="/wiki/FieldTurf" title="FieldTurf">FieldTurf</a> surface for an existing intramurals field.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies" title="Washington Huskies">Washington Huskies</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg/170px-Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg/255px-Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg/340px-Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Huskies_defense.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Washington Huskies football team
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UW students, sports teams, and alumni are called <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies" title="Washington Huskies">Washington Huskies</a>, and often referred to <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">metonymically</a> as &quot;Montlake,&quot; due to the campus's location on Montlake Boulevard N.E.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> (It should be noted that the traditional bounds of the <a href="/wiki/Montlake,_Seattle,_Washington" title="Montlake, Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">Montlake neighborhood</a> do <i>not</i> extend north of the <a href="/wiki/Montlake_Cut" title="Montlake Cut">Montlake Cut</a> to include the campus.) The <a href="/wiki/Husky" title="Husky">husky</a> was selected as the school mascot by student committee in 1922. It replaced the &quot;Sun Dodger,&quot; an abstract reference to the <a href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington#Climate" title="Seattle, Washington" class="mw-redirect">local weather</a> that was quickly dropped in favor of something more tangible. The costumed &quot;Harry the Husky&quot; performs at sporting and special events, and a live <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Malamute" title="Alaskan Malamute">Alaskan Malamute</a>, currently named Dubs, has traditionally led the UW <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team onto the field at the start of games. The school colors of purple and gold were adopted in 1892 by student vote. The choice was inspired by the first <a href="/wiki/Stanza" title="Stanza">stanza</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Destruction_of_Sennacherib" title="The Destruction of Sennacherib">The Destruction of Sennacherib</a></i>:<sup id="cite_ref-SchoolColors_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolColors-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <div class="poem"> 
       <p>The <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> came down like the wolf on the fold,<br /> And his cohorts were gleaming in purple and gold;<br /> And the sheen of their spears was like stars on the sea,<br /> When the blue wave rolls nightly on deep <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee" title="Sea of Galilee">Galilee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SchoolColors_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolColors-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
      </div> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>The sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a>'s Division I-A and in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. Among its facilities on campus are <a href="/wiki/Husky_Stadium" title="Husky Stadium">Husky Stadium</a> (football, track and field), the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines_Arena_at_Hec_Edmundson_Pavilion" title="Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion">Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion</a> (basketball, volleyball, and gymnastics), <a href="/wiki/Husky_Ballpark" title="Husky Ballpark">Husky Ballpark</a> (baseball), Husky Softball Stadium, The <a href="/wiki/William_Quillian_(athlete)" title="William Quillian (athlete)" class="mw-redirect">Bill Quillian Tennis Stadium</a>, The <a href="/wiki/Nordstrom" title="Nordstrom">Nordstrom</a> Tennis Center, Dempsey Indoor (Indoor track and field, football) and the Conibear Shellhouse (rowing). The golf team plays at the Washington National Golf Club and until recently, the swimming team called the <a href="/wiki/Weyerhaeuser" title="Weyerhaeuser">Weyerhaeuser</a> Aquatic Center and the Husky pool home. (The university eliminated its men's and women's swim teams in May, 2009.) <sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_football" title="Washington Huskies football">University football team</a> is traditionally competitive, having won the 1960 and 1991 national title, to go along with eight <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(game)" title="Rose Bowl (game)" class="mw-redirect">Rose Bowl</a> victories and an <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl_(game)" title="Orange Bowl (game)" class="mw-redirect">Orange Bowl</a> title. From 1907 to 1917, Washington football teams were unbeaten in 63 consecutive games, an <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> record.<sup id="cite_ref-unbeaten_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unbeaten-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tailgate_party" title="Tailgate party">Tailgating</a> by boat has been a Husky Stadium tradition since 1920 when the stadium was first built on the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Washington" title="Lake Washington">Lake Washington</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Apple_Cup" title="Apple Cup">Apple Cup</a> game is an annual game against cross-state rival <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a> that was first contested in 1900 with UW leading the all-time series, 65 wins to 31 losses and 6 ties. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Sarkisian" title="Steve Sarkisian">Steve Sarkisian</a> is the current head football coach.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hec_Ed.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/220px-Hec_Ed.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/330px-Hec_Ed.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Hec_Ed.JPG/440px-Hec_Ed.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hec_Ed.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Airlines_Arena_at_Hec_Edmundson_Pavilion" title="Alaska Airlines Arena at Hec Edmundson Pavilion">Hec Edmundson Pavilion</a> is used for basketball and volleyball.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The men's <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_men%27s_basketball" title="Washington Huskies men's basketball">basketball</a> team has been moderately successful, though recently the team has enjoyed a resurgence under coach <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Romar" title="Lorenzo Romar">Lorenzo Romar</a>. With Romar as head coach, the team has been to six <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA tournaments</a> (2003?2004, 2004?2005, 2005?2006, 2008?2009, 2009?2010 and 2010?2011 seasons), 2 consecutive top 16 (sweet sixteen) appearances, and secured a No. 1 seed in 2005. On December 23, 2005, the men's basketball team won their 800th victory in Hec Edmundson Pavilion, the most wins for any NCAA team in its current arena.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/College_rowing_(United_States)" title="College rowing (United States)">Rowing</a> is a longstanding tradition at the University of Washington dating back to 1901. The Washington men's crew gained international prominence by winning the <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics" title="1936 Summer Olympics">1936 Summer Olympics</a> in Berlin, defeating the German and Italian crews much to the chagrin of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> who was in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1958, the men's crew furthered their lore with a shocking win over <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Leningrad</a> Trud's world champion rowers at the Moscow Cup, resulting in the first American sporting victory on <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> soil,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and certainly the first time a <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> crowd gave any American team a standing ovation during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The men's crew have won 46 national titles<sup id="cite_ref-RowingSuccessful_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RowingSuccessful-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> (15 <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a>, 1 <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Rowing_Championship" title="National Collegiate Rowing Championship">National Collegiate Rowing Championship</a>), 15 Olympic gold medals, two silver and five bronze. The women have 10 national titles and two Olympic gold medals. In 1997, the women's team won the NCAA championship.<sup id="cite_ref-RowingSuccessful_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RowingSuccessful-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The Husky men are the 2012 national champions.</p> 
     <p>Recent national champions include the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Huskies_softball" title="Washington Huskies softball">softball</a> team (<a href="/wiki/2009_Women%27s_College_World_Series" title="2009 Women's College World Series">2009</a>), the men's rowing team (2012, 2011, 2009, 2007), NCAA Division I women's <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> team (2008), and the women's volleyball team (<a href="/wiki/2005_NCAA_Division_I_Women%27s_Volleyball_Tournament" title="2005 NCAA Division I Women's Volleyball Tournament">2005</a>). Individually, Scott Roth was the 2011 NCAA men's Outdoor <a href="/wiki/Pole_Vault" title="Pole Vault" class="mw-redirect">Pole Vault</a> and 2011 &amp; 2010 NCAA men's Indoor Pole Vault champion. <a href="/wiki/James_Lepp" title="James Lepp">James Lepp</a> was the 2005 NCAA men's golf champion. Ryan Brown (men's 800 meters) and Amy Lia (women's 1500 meters) won individual titles at the 2006 NCAA Track and Field Championships. <a href="/wiki/Brad_Walker_(athlete)" title="Brad Walker (athlete)">Brad Walker</a> was the 2005 NCAA men's Outdoor and Indoor Pole Vault champion.</p> 
     <p>Husky Stadium is one of several places that may have been the birthplace of the crowd phenomenon known as &quot;<a href="/wiki/Audience_wave" title="Audience wave" class="mw-redirect">The Wave</a>&quot;. It is claimed that the wave was invented in October 1981 by Husky graduate Robb Weller and UW band director Bill Bissel. Their opponent that night was Stanford.</p> 
     <p>On May 1, 2009, the athletic department announced it was discontinuing both men's and women's swimming programs effective immediately due to budget cuts.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Husky_Stadium">Husky Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Husky Stadium">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Husky_Stadium" title="Husky Stadium">Husky Stadium</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg/220px-Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg/330px-Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg/440px-Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_Husky_Stadium_March_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An aerial view of Husky Stadium in 2009
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The new Husky Stadium is the first and primary income source of a completely remodeled athletic district. This major remodel of the athletic village will take decades to complete, as it will take place at the same time as a massive project by the Washington State Department of Transportation on nearby highways and bridges. The stadium project consists of a new grand concourse, underground light-rail station, enclosed west end of the stadium, replacement of bleachers with individual seating, removal of track and Huskytron, new press box, private box seating, lowering of the field, football offices, permanent seating in the east end zone that does not block the view of Lake Washington, and new and improved amenities, concession stands and bathrooms throughout. In addition, the concession areas will be constructed to face inward, allowing spectators to view the game through the main concourse which will circle around the field. Along with the Husky Stadium remodel, new parking garages will be constructed and renovated facilities throughout the athletic village.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The stadium has developed numerous structural problems, particularly in the lower bowl, caused by age and the continually moist weather. Renovation plans are slated to begin in November 2011. The project was approved by University of Washington regents in November 2010 at a cost of $250 million.</p> 
     <p>Several drawings by <a href="/wiki/Populous_(architects)" title="Populous (architects)" class="mw-redirect">Populous</a> (formerly HOK Sport) have been released depicting what the future Husky Stadium might look like.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_services">Student services</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Student services">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The UW offers many services for its students and alumni, even beyond the standard offered by most colleges and universities. Its &quot;Student Life&quot; division houses 16 departments and offices that serve students directly and indirectly, including those below and overseen by Vice President and Vice Provost, Eric Godfrey?</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The UW Career Center</li> 
      <li>Counseling Center</li> 
     </ul> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Meany_Hall,_University_of_Washington.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/220px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/330px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg/440px-Meany_Hall%2C_University_of_Washington.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Meany_Hall,_University_of_Washington.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Meany Hall, Concert Hall of University of Washington
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Disability Resource Center</li> 
      <li>Fraternity and Sorority Life</li> 
      <li>Health and Wellness Programs</li> 
      <li>Housing and Food Services</li> 
      <li>Student Admissions</li>

      <li>Department of Recreational Sports (IMA)</li>
