     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>New building construction and renovations are scheduled to take place through 2020. The plan includes the construction of three six-story residence halls and two apartment complexes in the west section of campus, near the existing <a href="/wiki/Terry_and_Lander_Halls" title="Terry and Lander Halls">Terry and Lander Halls</a>, in Phase I, the renovation of six existing residence halls in Phase II, and additional new construction in Phase III. The projects will result in a net gain of approximately 2,400 beds.</p> 
     <p>In addition to on-campus housing the undergraduate student government, Associated Students of the University Washington, provides a free service to students, faculty, and staff looking to live off-campus called Off-Campus Housing Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> They provide a free online search engine to local housing and resources to assist first time renters.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UW_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/220px-UW_Tower.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/330px-UW_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/UW_Tower.jpg/440px-UW_Tower.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UW_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University of Washington Tower, 99 Meters high with 22 Stories
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Many of the sustainable changes at the University of Washington have resulted from campus activism. Several environmental-activism groups on campus include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Rural Health Education (RHE): Promotes health in rural areas of Washington state primarily through monthly health fairs. Volunteers include students from a variety of backgrounds including: medical, pharmacy, and dental students. In addition, several health professionals from around the greater Seattle area actively participate.</li> 
      <li>Students Expressing Environmental Dedication (SEED): SEED works with Housing and Food Services to increase the sustainability of the residence halls and dining areas.</li> 
      <li>UW Earth Club: The Earth Club is interested in promoting the expression of environmental attitudes and consciousness through specialized events.</li> 
      <li>UW Farm: The UW farm grows crops on campus and advocates urban farming in the UW community.</li> 
      <li>Washington Public Interest Research Group (WashPIRG): WashPIRG engages students in a variety of activism causes, including environmental projects on campus and the community.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>UW Sierra Student Coalition: SSC is dedicated to many larger environmental issues on campus and providing related opportunities to students.</li> 
      <li>UW Delta Delta Sigma Pre-Dental Society (DDS): This is a club dedicated to serving pre-dental students and it provides a forum for discussion of dental related topics.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disability_support">Disability support</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Disability support">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/The_DO-IT_Center" title="The DO-IT Center">DO-IT (Disabilities, Opportunities, Internetworking, and Technology) Center</a> is a program run by the university which assists educational institutions to fully integrate all students, including those with disabilities, into Academic life. DO-IT runs many programs, including the <a href="/wiki/DO-IT_Scholars_Program" title="DO-IT Scholars Program">DO-IT Scholars Program</a>, and a database of information on the 'universal' design of educational facilities for students of all levels of physical and mental ability.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> These design programs reduce systemic barriers which could otherwise hinder the performance of some students. DO-IT's universal design philosophies may also be applied to professional organizations and conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Song">Song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington_Husky_Marching_Band" title="University of Washington Husky Marching Band">University of Washington Husky Marching Band</a> performs at many Husky sporting events including all <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> games. The band was founded in 1929, and today it is a cornerstone of Husky spirit. The band marches using a traditional high step, and it is one of only a few marching bands left in the United States to do so. Like many college bands, the Husky band has several traditional songs that it has played for decades, including the official <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight songs</a> &quot;<a href="/wiki/Bow_Down_to_Washington" title="Bow Down to Washington">Bow Down to Washington</a>&quot; and &quot;<a href="/wiki/Tequila_(song)" title="Tequila (song)">Tequila</a>&quot;, as well as fan-favorite &quot;Africano&quot;. In addition to athletic events, the band also plays at various other events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_the_Husky" title="Harry the Husky">Harry the Husky</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Basketball_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/170px-Basketball_1.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/255px-Basketball_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Basketball_1.JPG/340px-Basketball_1.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Basketball_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The previous costumed Harry the Husky at a school basketball game.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Washington's costumed mascot is <a href="/wiki/Harry_the_Husky" title="Harry the Husky">Harry the Husky</a>.</p> 
     <p>The University of Washington also has hosted a long line of <a href="/wiki/Alaskan_Malamute" title="Alaskan Malamute">Alaskan Malamutes</a> as mascots. The 13 dogs thus far have been:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Frosty I (1922?29)</li> 
      <li>Frosty II (1930?36)</li> 
      <li>Wasky (1946)</li> 
      <li>Wasky II (1947?53)</li> 
      <li>Ski (1954?57)</li> 
      <li>Denali (1958)</li> 
      <li>King Chinook (1959?68)</li> 
      <li>Regent Denali (1969?80)</li> 
      <li>Sundodger (1981?91)</li> 
      <li>King Redoubt (1992?97)</li> 
      <li>Prince Redoubt (1998)</li> 
      <li>Spirit (1999?2008)</li> 
      <li>Dubs (2009?)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Originally the dogs were cared for by the <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon" title="Sigma Alpha Epsilon">Sigma Alpha Epsilon</a> fraternity, followed by a 49 year tradition (1959?2008) of care by the Cross family (a UW professor followed by his son).</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Washington&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Then UW President Emmert signed the American College and University Presidents Climate Commitment.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> To help follow through on this promise, the UW has created a Climate Action Team.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> He has also created an Environmental Stewardship Advisory Committee (ESAC), which recently created an inventory of UW's greenhouse gas emissions,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> an environmental stewardship coordinator position, and has formalized a policy on environmental stewardship to give full institutional support to the cause of campus sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Stewardship_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Stewardship-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of February 2006, the UW joined a partnership with Seattle City Light as part of their Green Up Program. All of Seattle campus' electricity is purchased from renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Housing and Food Services (HFS) spends several million dollars annually on locally produced, organic, and natural foods. HFS does not use styrofoam containers for any of its facilities on campus, instead using compostable cups, plates, utensils, and packaging whenever possible. Students Expressing Environmental Concern (SEED) is funded by HFS and is responsible for most of the sustainable changes made to HFS. Several new residence halls are planned for 2020, all of which are expected to meet silver or gold LEED standards.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> All new state-funded buildings and major renovations must meet a <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> standard of at least Silver.<sup id="cite_ref-uwnews.org_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwnews.org-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Washington was one of only six universities to receive the highest grade on the Sustainable Endowments Institute's College Sustainability Report Card 2008, an &quot;A-&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The report card identified the UW as one of 15 Overall College Sustainability Leaders among the 300 institutions surveyed.<sup id="cite_ref-uwnews.org_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwnews.org-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Todd Photographs Collection</a> includes images from 1905?1930 of the University of Washington campus and scenes from Seattle including the waterfront, various buildings especially apartments, <a href="/wiki/Regrading" title="Regrading">regrading</a> activities, and the Pike Place Market.</li> 
      <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://content.lib.washington.edu/uwcampusweb/index.html">University of Washington Libraries Digital Collections ? University of Washington Campus Photographs</a> Photographs reflecting the early history of the University of Washington campus from its beginnings as the Territorial University through its establishment at its present site on the shores of Lake Washington. The database documents student activities, buildings, departments, and athletics.</li>
